modern city with <a href="/wiki/Rhacotis" title="Rhacotis">at least</a> 23 centuries of <a href="/wiki/History_of_Alexandria" title="History of Alexandria">history</a>.</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Eastasia_lights.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1498" data-file-width="1556" illumination. Here the <a href="/wiki/Taiheiy%C5%8D_Belt" title="Taiheiy&#333; Belt">Taiheiy&#333; Belt</a>, which includes Tokyo, demonstrates how <a href="/wiki/Megalopolis" title="Megalopolis">megalopolises</a> can lighting.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1"><a href="#cite_note-1">[1]</a></sup></div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Piraeus_map_1908.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="454" data-file-width="609" decoding="async" height="224" href="/wiki/File:Piraeus_map_1908.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>This 1908 map of <a href="/wiki/Piraeus" title="Piraeus">Piraeus</a>, the port of <a href="/wiki/Athens" title="Athens">Athens</a>, shows the city\'s <a href="/wiki/Grid_plan" title="Grid plan">grid plan</a>, credited by <a href="/wiki/Aristotle" title="Aristotle">Aristotle</a> to <a href="/wiki/Hippodamus_of_Miletus" title="Hippodamus of Miletus">Hippodamus of Miletus</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-crabgrass_3-0"><a href="#cite_note-crabgrass-3">[3]</a></sup></div></div></div>\n<p>A <b>city</b> is a large <a href="/wiki/Human_settlement" title="Human settlement">human settlement</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Goodall_4-0"><a href="#cite_note-Goodall-4">[4]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kuper_and_Kuper_5-0"><a href="#cite_note-Kuper_and_Kuper-5">[5]</a></sup> Cities generally have extensive systems for <a href="/wiki/Housing" title="Housing">housing</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Transportation" title="Transportation">transportation</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sanitation" title="Sanitation">sanitation</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Public_utilities" title="Public utilities">utilities</a>, <a href="/wiki/Land_use" title="Land use">land use</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Communication" title="Communication">communication</a>. Their density facilitates interaction between people, government organizations and businesses, sometimes benefiting different parties in the process.\n</p><p>Historically, city-dwellers have been a small proportion of humanity overall, but following two centuries of unprecedented and rapid <a href="/wiki/Urbanization" title="Urbanization">urbanization</a>, roughly half of the <a href="/wiki/World_population" title="World population">world population</a> now lives in cities, which has had profound consequences for global sustainability.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup> Present-day cities usually form the core of larger <a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_area" title="Metropolitan area">metropolitan areas</a> and <a href="/wiki/Urban_area" title="Urban area">urban areas</a>&#8212;creating numerous <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Commuter" title="Commuter">commuters</a> traveling towards <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/City_center" title="City center">city centers</a> for employment, entertainment, and edification. However, in a world of intensifying <a href="/wiki/Globalization" title="Globalization">globalization</a>, all cities are in different degree also connected globally beyond these regions.\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/List_of_largest_cities" title="List of largest cities">most populated</a> <a href="/wiki/City_proper" title="City proper">city proper</a> is <a href="/wiki/Chongqing" title="Chongqing">Chongqing</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup> while the <a href="/wiki/List_of_metropolitan_areas_by_population" title="List of metropolitan areas by population">most populous metropolitan areas</a> are the <a href="/wiki/Greater_Tokyo_Area" title="Greater Tokyo Area">Greater Tokyo Area</a>, the Shanghai area, and <a href="/wiki/Jabodetabek" title="Jabodetabek">Jabodetabek</a> (<a href="/wiki/Jakarta" title="Jakarta">Jakarta</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup> The cities of <a href="/wiki/Faiyum" title="Faiyum">Faiyum</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Damascus" title="Damascus">Damascus</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Varanasi" title="Varanasi">Varanasi</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup> are among those laying claim to <a href="/wiki/List_of_oldest_continuously_inhabited_cities" title="List of oldest continuously inhabited cities">longest continual inhabitation</a>.\n</p>\n<div class="toc" id="toc"><input class="toctogglecheckbox" id="toctogglecheckbox" role="button" style="display:none" type="checkbox"/><div class="toctitle" dir="ltr" class="toctext">Global governance</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-34"><a href="#United_Nations_System"><span class="tocnumber">9.4</span> <span class="toctext">United Nations System</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-35"><a href="#Representation_in_culture"><span class="tocnumber">10</span> <span class="toctext">Representation in culture</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-36"><a href="#See_also"><span class="tocnumber">11</span> <span class="toctext">See also</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-37"><a href="#Notes"><span class="tocnumber">12</span> <span class="toctext">Notes</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-38"><a href="#References"><span class="tocnumber">13</span> <span class="toctext">References</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-39"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">14</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Meaning">Meaning</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=City&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Meaning">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Sheth_Motisha_Tonk_01.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2985" data-file-width="4359" decoding="async" height="205" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Sheth_Motisha_Tonk_01.jpg/300px-Sheth_Motisha_Tonk_01.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Sheth_Motisha_Tonk_01.jpg/450px-Sheth_Motisha_Tonk_01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Sheth_Motisha_Tonk_01.jpg/600px-Sheth_Motisha_Tonk_01.jpg 2x" width="300"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Sheth_Motisha_Tonk_01.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Palitana" title="Palitana">Palitana</a> represents the city\'s symbolic function in the extreme, devoted as it is to <a href="/wiki/Palitana_temples" title="Palitana temples">Jain temples</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup></div></div></div>\n<p>A city is distinguished from other human settlements by its relatively great size, but also by its functions and its <a href="/wiki/City_status" title="City status">special symbolic status</a>, which may be conferred by a central authority. The term can also refer either to the physical streets and buildings of the city or to the collection of people who dwell there, and can be used in a general sense to mean urban rather than rural territory.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-OED_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-OED-13">[13]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lynch2008p678_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-Lynch2008p678-14">[14]</a></sup>\n</p><p>A variety of definitions, invoking <a href="/wiki/Population" title="Population">population</a>, <a href="/wiki/Population_density" title="Population density">population density</a>, number of <a href="/wiki/Dwelling" title="Dwelling">dwellings</a>, economic function, and <a href="/wiki/Infrastructure" title="Infrastructure">infrastructure</a>, are used in national <a href="/wiki/Census" title="Census">censuses</a> to classify populations as urban. Common population definitions for a city range between 1,500 and 50,000 people, with most U.S. states using a minimum between 1,500 and 5,000 inhabitants.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HugoEtAl2003_16-0"><a href="#cite_note-HugoEtAl2003-16">[16]</a></sup>  However, some jurisdictions set no such minimums.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/City_status_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="City status in the United Kingdom">In the United Kingdom</a>, city status is awarded by the government and then remains permanently, resulting in some very small cities, such as <a href="/wiki/Wells,_Somerset" title="Wells, Somerset">Wells</a> and <a href="/wiki/St_Davids" title="St Davids">St Davids</a>. According to the "functional definition" a city is not distinguished by size alone, but also by the role it plays within a larger political context. Cities serve as administrative, commercial, religious, and cultural hubs for their larger surrounding areas.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Smith2002_18-0"><a href="#cite_note-Smith2002-18">[18]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Marshall14_19-0"><a href="#cite_note-Marshall14-19">[19]</a></sup> Examples of settlements called city which may not meet any of the traditional criteria to be named such include <a href="/wiki/Broad_Top_City,_Pennsylvania" title="Broad Top City, Pennsylvania">Broad Top City, Pennsylvania</a> (pop 452), and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/City_Dulas" title="City Dulas">City Dulas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Anglesey" title="Anglesey">Anglesey</a>, a hamlet.\n</p><p>The presence of a <a href="/wiki/Intelligentsia" title="Intelligentsia">literate elite</a> is sometimes included in the definition.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup> A typical city has professional <a href="/wiki/Management" title="Management">administrators</a>, regulations, and some form of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Taxation" title="Taxation">taxation</a> (food and other necessities or means to trade for them) to feed the <a href="/wiki/Civil_service" title="Civil service">government workers</a>. (This arrangement contrasts with the more typically <a href="/wiki/Egalitarianism" title="Egalitarianism">horizontal</a> relationships in a <a href="/wiki/Tribe" title="Tribe">tribe</a> or <a href="/wiki/Village" title="Village">village</a> accomplishing common goals through informal agreements between neighbors, or through leadership of a chief.) The governments may be based on heredity, religion, military power, work projects such as canal building, food distribution, land ownership, agriculture, commerce, manufacturing, finance, or a combination of these. Societies that live in cities are often called <a href="/wiki/Civilization" title="Civilization">civilizations</a>.\n</p><p>The word <i>city</i> and the related <i><a href="/wiki/Civilization" title="Civilization">civilization</a></i> come, via Old French, from the Latin root <i><a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/civitas" title="wikt:civitas">civitas</a></i>, originally meaning citizenship or community member and eventually coming to correspond with <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/urbs" title="wikt:urbs">urbs</a>, meaning city in a more physical sense.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-OED_13-1"><a href="#cite_note-OED-13">[13]</a></sup> The Roman <i>civitas</i> was closely linked with the Greek "<a href="/wiki/Polis" title="Polis">polis</a>"&#8212;another common root appearing in English words such as <i><a href="/wiki/Metropolis" title="Metropolis">metropolis</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=City&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Kartie_Sakhali_old_grave_yard_-_panoramio_-_Masoud_Akbari.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="768" //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Kartie_Sakhali_old_grave_yard_-_panoramio_-_Masoud_Akbari.jpg/440px-Kartie_Sakhali_old_grave_yard_-_panoramio_-_Masoud_Akbari.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Kartie_Sakhali_old_grave_yard_-_panoramio_-_Masoud_Akbari.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Hillside housing and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Graveyard" title="Graveyard">graveyard</a> in Kabul.</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tnone" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right:auto; width:auto; max-width:1008px;">\n<div class="thumbinner"><div class="noresize overflowbugx" style="overflow:auto;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Tirana_Albania_pano_2004-07-14.jpg" title="Panoramic view of Albania from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mount_Dajt" title="Mount Dajt">Mount Dajt</a> in 2004.</div>\n</div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Allegheny_Monongahela_Ohio.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="918" data-file-width="1446" decoding="async" height="140" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Allegheny_Monongahela_Ohio.jpg/330px-Allegheny_Monongahela_Ohio.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Allegheny_Monongahela_Ohio.jpg/440px-Allegheny_Monongahela_Ohio.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Allegheny_Monongahela_Ohio.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Downtown_Pittsburgh" title="Downtown Pittsburgh">Downtown Pittsburgh</a> sits at the <a href="/wiki/Confluence" title="Confluence">confluence</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Monongahela_River" title="Monongahela River">Monongahela</a> and <a href="/wiki/Allegheny_River" title="Allegheny River">Allegheny</a> rivers, which become the <a href="/wiki/Ohio_River" title="Ohio River">Ohio</a>.</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:L%27Enfant_plan.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3404" data-file-width="4179" decoding="async" height="179" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/L%27Enfant_plan.jpg/220px-L%27Enfant_plan.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/L%27Enfant_plan.jpg/330px-L%27Enfant_plan.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/L%27Enfant_plan.jpg/440px-L%27Enfant_plan.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:L%27Enfant_plan.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/L%27Enfant_Plan" title="L\'Enfant Plan">L\'Enfant Plan</a> for <a href="/wiki/Washington,_D.C." title="Washington, D.C.">Washington, D.C.</a>, inspired by the design of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Versailles" title="Versailles">Versailles</a>, combines a utilitarian grid pattern with diagonal avenues and a symbolic focus on <a href="/wiki/Monument" title="Monument">monumental</a> architecture.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup></div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:282px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Tel_Aviv,_Israel_by_Planet_Labs.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2775" data-file-width="3700" decoding="async" height="210" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Tel_Aviv%2C_Israel_by_Planet_Labs.jpg/280px-Tel_Aviv%2C_Israel_by_Planet_Labs.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Tel_Aviv%2C_Israel_by_Planet_Labs.jpg/420px-Tel_Aviv%2C_Israel_by_Planet_Labs.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Tel_Aviv%2C_Israel_by_Planet_Labs.jpg/560px-Tel_Aviv%2C_Israel_by_Planet_Labs.jpg 2x" width="280"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Tel_Aviv,_Israel_by_Planet_Labs.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>This aerial view of the <a href="/wiki/Gush_Dan" title="Gush Dan">Gush Dan</a> metropolitan area in Israel shows the geometrically planned<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> city of <a href="/wiki/Tel_Aviv" title="Tel Aviv">Tel Aviv</a> proper (upper left) as well as <a href="/wiki/Givatayim" title="Givatayim">Givatayim</a> to the east and some of <a href="/wiki/Bat_Yam" title="Bat Yam">Bat Yam</a> to the south. Tel Aviv\'s population is 433,000; the total population of its metropolitan area is 3,785,000.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup></div></div></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Urban_geography" title="Urban geography">Urban geography</a> deals both with cities in their larger context and with their internal structure.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Site">Site</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=City&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Site">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Town siting has varied through history according to natural, technological, economic, and military contexts. Access to water has long been a major factor in city placement and growth, and despite exceptions enabled by the advent of <a href="/wiki/Rail_transport" title="Rail transport">rail transport</a> in the nineteenth century, through the present most of the world\'s urban population lives near the coast or on a river.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Urban areas as a rule cannot <a href="/wiki/Subsistence_agriculture" title="Subsistence agriculture">produce their own food</a> and therefore must develop some <a href="/wiki/City_region" title="City region">relationship</a> with a <a href="/wiki/Hinterland" title="Hinterland">hinterland</a> which sustains them.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kaplan2004p155_27-0"><a href="#cite_note-Kaplan2004p155-27">[27]</a></sup> Only in special cases such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mining_town" title="Mining town">mining towns</a> which play a vital role in long-distance trade, are cities disconnected from the countryside which feeds them.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Marshall1989p15_28-0"><a href="#cite_note-Marshall1989p15-28">[28]</a></sup> Thus, centrality within a productive region influences siting, as economic forces would in theory favor the creation of market places in optimal mutually reachable locations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Latham2009p18_29-0"><a href="#cite_note-Latham2009p18-29">[29]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Center">Center</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=City&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Center">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/City_centre" title="City centre">City centre</a></div>\n<p>The vast majority of cities have a central area containing buildings with special economic, political, and religious significance. Archaeologists refer to this area by the Greek term <a href="/wiki/Temenos" title="Temenos">temenos</a> or if fortified as a <a href="/wiki/Citadel" title="Citadel">citadel</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup> These spaces historically reflect and amplify the city\'s centrality and importance to its wider <a href="/wiki/City_region" title="City region">sphere of influence</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Latham2009p18_29-1"><a href="#cite_note-Latham2009p18-29">[29]</a></sup> Today cities have a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/City_center" title="City center">city center</a> or <a href="/wiki/Downtown" title="Downtown">downtown</a>, sometimes coincident with a <a href="/wiki/Central_business_district" title="Central business district">central business district</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Public_space">Public space</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=City&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Public space">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Cities typically have <a href="/wiki/Public_space" title="Public space">public spaces</a> where anyone can go. These include <a href="/wiki/Privately_owned_public_space" title="Privately owned public space">privately owned spaces open to the public</a> as well as forms of public land such as <a href="/wiki/Public_domain_(land)" title="Public domain (land)">public domain</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Common_land" title="Common land">commons</a>. <a href="/wiki/Western_philosophy" title="Western philosophy">Western philosophy</a> since the time of the Greek <a href="/wiki/Agora" title="Agora">agora</a> has considered physical public space as the substrate of the symbolic <a href="/wiki/Public_sphere" title="Public sphere">public sphere</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Public_art" title="Public art">Public art</a> adorns (or disfigures) public spaces. <a href="/wiki/Park" title="Park">Parks</a> and other <a href="/wiki/Incorporation_of_nature_within_a_city" title="Incorporation of nature within a city">natural sites within cities</a> provide residents with relief from the hardness and regularity of typical <a href="/wiki/Built_environment" title="Built environment">built environments</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Internal_structure">Internal structure</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=City&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Internal structure">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Urban_structure" title="Urban structure">Urban structure</a> generally follows one or more basic patterns: geomorphic, radial, concentric, rectilinear, and curvilinear. Physical environment generally constrains the form in which a city is built. If located on a mountainside, urban structure may rely on terraces and winding roads. It may be adapted to its means of subsistence (e.g. agriculture or fishing). And it may be set up for optimal defense given the surrounding landscape.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup> Beyond these "geomorphic" features, cities can develop internal patterns, due to natural growth or to <a href="/wiki/Urban_planning" title="Urban planning">city planning</a>.\n</p><p>In a radial structure, main roads converge on a central point. This form could evolve from successive growth over a long time, with concentric traces of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Town_wall" title="Town wall">town walls</a> and <a href="/wiki/Citadel" title="Citadel">citadels</a> marking older city boundaries. In more recent history, such forms were supplemented by <a href="/wiki/Ring_road" title="Ring road">ring roads</a> moving traffic around the outskirts of a town. Dutch cities such as <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam" title="Amsterdam">Amsterdam</a> and <a href="/wiki/Haarlem" title="Haarlem">Haarlem</a> are structured as a central square surrounded by concentric canals marking every expansion. In cities such as and also <a href="/wiki/Moscow" title="Moscow">Moscow</a>, this pattern is still clearly visible.\n</p><p>A system of rectilinear city streets and land plots, known as the <a href="/wiki/Grid_plan" title="Grid plan">grid plan</a>, has been used for millennia in Asia, Europe, and the Americas.  The <a href="/wiki/Indus_Valley_Civilisation" title="Indus Valley Civilisation">Indus Valley Civilisation</a> built <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mohenjo-Daro" title="Mohenjo-Daro">Mohenjo-Daro</a>, <a href="/wiki/Harappa" title="Harappa">Harappa</a> and other cities on a grid pattern, using ancient principles described by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kautilya" title="Kautilya">Kautilya</a>, and aligned with the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Compass_points" title="Compass points">compass points</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Smith2002_18-1"><a href="#cite_note-Smith2002-18">[18]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> The ancient Greek city of <a href="/wiki/Priene" title="Priene">Priene</a> exemplifies a grid plan with specialized districts used across the <a href="/wiki/Hellenistic_period" title="Hellenistic period">Hellenistic Mediterranean</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Urban_areas">Urban areas</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=City&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Urban areas">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Urban-type settlement extends far beyond the traditional boundaries of the <a href="/wiki/City_proper" title="City proper">city proper</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup> in a form of development sometimes described critically as <a href="/wiki/Urban_sprawl" title="Urban sprawl">urban sprawl</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup> Decentralization and dispersal of city functions (commercial, industrial, residential, cultural, political) has transformed the very meaning of the term and has challenged geographers seeking to classify territories according to an urban-rural binary.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HugoEtAl2003_16-1"><a href="#cite_note-HugoEtAl2003-16">[16]</a></sup>\n</p><p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Metropolitan_areas" title="Metropolitan areas">Metropolitan areas</a> include <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Suburbs" title="Suburbs">suburbs</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Exurbs" title="Exurbs">exurbs</a> organized around the needs of <a href="/wiki/Commuting" title="Commuting">commuters</a>, and sometimes <a href="/wiki/Edge_city" title="Edge city">edge cities</a> characterized by a degree of economic and political independence. (In the US these are grouped into <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Metropolitan_statistical_areas" title="Metropolitan statistical areas">metropolitan statistical areas</a> for purposes of <a href="/wiki/Demography" title="Demography">demography</a> and <a href="/wiki/Marketing" title="Marketing">marketing</a>.) Some cities are now part of a continuous urban landscape called <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Urban_agglomeration" title="Urban agglomeration">urban agglomeration</a>, <a href="/wiki/Conurbation" title="Conurbation">conurbation</a>, or <a href="/wiki/Megalopolis" title="Megalopolis">megalopolis</a> (exemplified by the <a href="/wiki/Northeast_megalopolis" title="Northeast megalopolis">BosWash</a> corridor of the Northeastern United States.)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=City&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_city" title="History of the city">History of the city</a></div>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Urban_history" title="Urban history">Urban history</a>, <a href="/wiki/Historical_urban_community_sizes" title="Historical urban community sizes">Historical urban community sizes</a>, and <a href="/wiki/List_of_largest_cities_throughout_history" title="List of largest cities throughout history">List of largest cities throughout history</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Oldest_arch_4.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2304" data-file-width="3072" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Oldest_arch_4.JPG/220px-Oldest_arch_4.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Oldest_arch_4.JPG/330px-Oldest_arch_4.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Oldest_arch_4.JPG/440px-Oldest_arch_4.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Oldest_arch_4.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>An <a href="/wiki/Arch" title="Arch">arch</a> from the ancient <a href="/wiki/Sumer" title="Sumer">Sumerian</a> city <a href="/wiki/Ur" title="Ur">Ur</a>, which flourished in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Third_millennium_BC" title="Third millennium BC">third millennium BC</a>, can be seen at present-day Tell el-Mukayyar in <a href="/wiki/Iraq" title="Iraq">Iraq</a></div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mohenjo-daro.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2736" data-file-width="3648" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Mohenjo-daro.jpg/220px-Mohenjo-daro.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Mohenjo-daro.jpg/330px-Mohenjo-daro.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Mohenjo-daro.jpg/440px-Mohenjo-daro.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Mohenjo-daro.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Mohenjo-daro" title="Mohenjo-daro">Mohenjo-daro</a>, a city of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Indus_Valley_Civilization" title="Indus Valley Civilization">Indus Valley Civilization</a>, which was rebuilt six or more times, using bricks of standard size, and adhering to the same grid layout&#8212;also in the third millennium BC.</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Teotihuac%C3%A1n_2012-09-28_00-07-11.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2328" data-file-width="3221" decoding="async" height="159" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/Teotihuac%C3%A1n_2012-09-28_00-07-11.jpg/220px-Teotihuac%C3%A1n_2012-09-28_00-07-11.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/Teotihuac%C3%A1n_2012-09-28_00-07-11.jpg/330px-Teotihuac%C3%A1n_2012-09-28_00-07-11.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/Teotihuac%C3%A1n_2012-09-28_00-07-11.jpg/440px-Teotihuac%C3%A1n_2012-09-28_00-07-11.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Teotihuac%C3%A1n_2012-09-28_00-07-11.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>This aerial view of what was once downtown <a href="/wiki/Teotihuacan" title="Teotihuacan">Teotihuacan</a> shows the <a href="/wiki/Pyramid_of_the_Sun" title="Pyramid of the Sun">Pyramid of the Sun</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pyramid_of_the_Moon" title="Pyramid of the Moon">Pyramid of the Moon</a>, and the processional avenue serving as the spine of the city\'s street system.</div></div></div>\n<p>Cities, characterized by <a href="/wiki/Population_density" title="Population density">population density</a>, <a href="/wiki/Symbol" title="Symbol">symbolic</a> function, and <a href="/wiki/Urban_planning" title="Urban planning">urban planning</a>, have existed for thousands of years. In the conventional view, civilization and the city both followed from the <a href="/wiki/Neolithic_Revolution" title="Neolithic Revolution">development of agriculture</a>, which enabled production of surplus food, and thus a social <a href="/wiki/Division_of_labour" title="Division of labour">division of labour</a> (with concomitant <a href="/wiki/Social_stratification" title="Social stratification">social stratification</a>) and <a href="/wiki/Trade" title="Trade">trade</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup> Early cities often featured <a href="/wiki/Granary" title="Granary">granaries</a>, sometimes within a temple.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup> A minority viewpoint considers that cities may have arisen without agriculture, due to alternative means of subsistence (fishing),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup> to use as communal seasonal shelters,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Perlman16_44-0"><a href="#cite_note-Perlman16-44">[44]</a></sup> to their value as bases for defensive and offensive military organization,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mumfurd1961war_45-0"><a href="#cite_note-Mumfurd1961war-45">[45]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ashworth1991p12_46-0"><a href="#cite_note-Ashworth1991p12-46">[46]</a></sup>  or to their inherent economic function.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jacobs_1969_23_47-0"><a href="#cite_note-Jacobs_1969_23-47">[47]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup> Cities played a crucial role in the establishment of political power over an area, and ancient leaders such as <a href="/wiki/Alexander_the_Great" title="Alexander the Great">Alexander the Great</a> founded and created them with zeal.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ancient_times">Ancient times</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=City&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Ancient times">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cities_of_the_Ancient_Near_East" title="Cities of the Ancient Near East">Cities of the Ancient Near East</a>, <a href="/wiki/Polis" title="Polis">Polis</a>, <a href="/wiki/City-state" title="City-state">City-state</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Late_Antiquity#Cities" title="Late Antiquity">Late Antiquity &#167;&#160;Cities</a></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Jericho" title="Jericho">Jericho</a> and <a href="/wiki/%C3%87atalh%C3%B6y%C3%BCk" title="&#199;atalh&#246;y&#252;k">&#199;atalh&#246;y&#252;k</a>, dated to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eighth_millennium_BC" title="Eighth millennium BC">eighth millennium BC</a>, are among the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Proto-cities" title="Proto-cities">earliest proto-cities</a> known to archaeologists.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Perlman16_44-1"><a href="#cite_note-Perlman16-44">[44]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup>\n</p><p>In the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fourth_millennium_BC" title="Fourth millennium BC">fourth</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Third_millennium_BC" title="Third millennium BC">third millennium BC</a>, complex civilizations flourished in the river valleys of <a href="/wiki/Mesopotamia" title="Mesopotamia">Mesopotamia</a>, <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a>, <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Egypt" title="Egypt">Egypt</a>. Excavations in these areas have found the <a href="/wiki/Ruins" title="Ruins">ruins</a> of cities geared variously towards trade, politics, or religion. Some had large, <a href="/wiki/Urban_density" title="Urban density">dense populations</a>, but others carried out urban activities in the realms of politics or religion without having large associated populations. Among the early Old World cities, <a href="/wiki/Mohenjo-daro" title="Mohenjo-daro">Mohenjo-daro</a> of the Indus Valley Civilization in present-day <a href="/wiki/Pakistan" title="Pakistan">Pakistan</a>, existing from about 2600 BC, was one of the largest, with a population of 50,000 or more and a <a href="/wiki/Sanitation_of_the_Indus_Valley_Civilisation" title="Sanitation of the Indus Valley Civilisation">sophisticated sanitation system</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Chinese_urban_planning" title="Ancient Chinese urban planning">China\'s planned cities</a> were constructed according to sacred principles to act as celestial <a href="/wiki/Macrocosm_and_microcosm" title="Macrocosm and microcosm">microcosms</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/List_of_ancient_Egyptian_towns_and_cities" title="List of ancient Egyptian towns and cities">Ancient Egyptian cities</a> known physically by archaeologists are not extensive.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Smith2002_18-2"><a href="#cite_note-Smith2002-18">[18]</a></sup> They include (known by their Arab names) <a href="/wiki/El_Lahun" title="El Lahun">El Lahun</a>, a workers\' town associated with the pyramid of <a href="/wiki/Senusret_II" title="Senusret II">Senusret II</a>, and the religious city <a href="/wiki/Amarna" title="Amarna">Amarna</a> built by <a href="/wiki/Akhenaten" title="Akhenaten">Akhenaten</a> and abandoned. These sites appear planned in a highly regimented and <a href="/wiki/Social_stratification" title="Social stratification">stratified</a> fashion, with a minimalistic grid of rooms for the workers and increasingly more elaborate housing available for higher classes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup>\n</p><p>In Mesopotamia, the civilization of <a href="/wiki/Sumer" title="Sumer">Sumer</a>, followed by <a href="/wiki/Assyria" title="Assyria">Assyria</a> and <a href="/wiki/Babylon" title="Babylon">Babylon</a>, gave rise to numerous cities, governed by kings and fostering multiple languages written in <a href="/wiki/Cuneiform" title="Cuneiform">cuneiform</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Phoenicia" title="Phoenicia">Phoenician</a> trading empire, flourishing around the turn of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/First_millennium_BC" title="First millennium BC">first millennium BC</a>, encompassed <a href="/wiki/List_of_Phoenician_cities" title="List of Phoenician cities">numerous cities</a> extending from <a href="/wiki/Tyre,_Lebanon" title="Tyre, Lebanon">Tyre</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cydon" title="Cydon">Cydon</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Byblos" title="Byblos">Byblos</a> to <a href="/wiki/Carthage" title="Carthage">Carthage</a> and <a href="/wiki/C%C3%A1diz" title="C&#225;diz">C&#225;diz</a>.\n</p><p>In the following centuries, independent <a href="/wiki/City-state" title="City-state">city-states</a> of <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Greece" title="Ancient Greece">Greece</a> developed the <i><a href="/wiki/Polis" title="Polis">polis</a></i>, an association of male landowning <a href="/wiki/Citizenship" title="Citizenship">citizens</a> who collectively constituted the city.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tws2Y21_56-0"><a href="#cite_note-tws2Y21-56">[56]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Agora" title="Agora">agora</a>, meaning "gathering place" or "assembly", was the center of athletic, artistic, spiritual and political life of the polis.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-InternationalDictionary_57-0"><a href="#cite_note-InternationalDictionary-57">[57]</a></sup> Rome\'s <a href="/wiki/Rise_of_Rome" title="Rise of Rome">rise to power</a> brought its population to one million. Under the authority of <a href="/wiki/Roman_Empire" title="Roman Empire">its empire</a>, Rome transformed and <a href="/wiki/List_of_cities_founded_by_the_Romans" title="List of cities founded by the Romans">founded</a> many cities (<i><a href="/wiki/Colonia_(Roman)" title="Colonia (Roman)">coloniae</a></i>), and with them brought its principles of urban architecture, design, and society.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup>\n</p><p>In the ancient Americas, early urban traditions developed in the <a href="/wiki/Andes" title="Andes">Andes</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mesoamerica" title="Mesoamerica">Mesoamerica</a>. In the Andes, the first urban centers developed in the <a href="/wiki/Norte_Chico_civilization" title="Norte Chico civilization">Norte Chico civilization</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chav%C3%ADn_culture" title="Chav&#237;n culture">Chavin</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Moche_(culture)" title="Moche (culture)">Moche</a> cultures, followed by major cities in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Huari_culture" title="Huari culture">Huari</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chimu" title="Chimu">Chimu</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Inca" title="Inca">Inca</a> cultures. The Norte Chico civilization included as many as 30 major population centers in what is now the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Norte_Chico_(Peruvian_region)" title="Norte Chico (Peruvian region)">Norte Chico region</a> of north-central coastal <a href="/wiki/Peru" title="Peru">Peru</a>. It is the oldest known civilization in the Americas, flourishing between the 30th century BC and the 18th century BC.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Shady1997_59-0"><a href="#cite_note-Shady1997-59">[59]</a></sup> Mesoamerica saw the rise of early urbanism in several cultural regions, beginning with the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Olmec" title="Olmec">Olmec</a> and spreading to the <a href="/wiki/Maya_city" title="Maya city">Preclassic Maya</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Zapotec_civilization" title="Zapotec civilization">Zapotec</a> of Oaxaca, and <a href="/wiki/Teotihuacan" title="Teotihuacan">Teotihuacan</a> in central Mexico. Later cultures such as the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Aztec" title="Aztec">Aztec</a> drew on these earlier urban traditions.\n</p><p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jenn%C3%A9-Jeno" title="Jenn&#233;-Jeno">Jenn&#233;-Jeno</a>, located in present-day Mali and dating to the third century BC,  lacked monumental architecture and a distinctive elite social class&#8212;but nevertheless had specialized production and relations with a hinterland.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup> Pre-Arabic trade contacts probably existed between Jenn&#233;-Jeno and North Africa.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Magnavita_61-0"><a href="#cite_note-Magnavita-61">[61]</a></sup> Other early urban centers in sub-Saharan Africa, dated to around 500 AD, include Awdaghust, Kumbi-Saleh the ancient capital of Ghana, and Maranda a center located on a trade route between Egypt and Gao.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup>\n</p><p>In the first millennium AD, <a href="/wiki/Angkor" title="Angkor">Angkor</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Khmer_Empire" title="Khmer Empire">Khmer Empire</a> grew into one of the most extensive cities in the world<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Evans_PNAS_63-0"><a href="#cite_note-Evans_PNAS-63">[63]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBC_News_2007_64-0"><a href="#cite_note-BBC_News_2007-64">[64]</a></sup> and may have supported up to one million people.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Middle_Ages">Middle Ages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=City&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Middle Ages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Holy_Roman_Empire_1648_Imperial_cities.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="595" data-file-width="681" decoding="async" height="192" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Holy_Roman_Empire_1648_Imperial_cities.png/220px-Holy_Roman_Empire_1648_Imperial_cities.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Holy_Roman_Empire_1648_Imperial_cities.png/330px-Holy_Roman_Empire_1648_Imperial_cities.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Holy_Roman_Empire_1648_Imperial_cities.png/440px-Holy_Roman_Empire_1648_Imperial_cities.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Holy_Roman_Empire_1648_Imperial_cities.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Imperial Free Cities in the Holy Roman Empire 1648</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Haarlem-City-Map-1550.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1332" data-file-width="1213" decoding="async" height="242" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Haarlem-City-Map-1550.jpg/220px-Haarlem-City-Map-1550.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Haarlem-City-Map-1550.jpg/330px-Haarlem-City-Map-1550.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Haarlem-City-Map-1550.jpg/440px-Haarlem-City-Map-1550.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Haarlem-City-Map-1550.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>This map of <a href="/wiki/Haarlem" title="Haarlem">Haarlem</a>, the Netherlands, created around 1550, shows the city completely surrounded by a <a href="/wiki/Defensive_wall" title="Defensive wall">city wall</a> and <a href="/wiki/Moat" title="Moat">defensive canal</a>, with its square shape inspired by <a href="/wiki/Jerusalem" title="Jerusalem">Jerusalem</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>In the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fall_of_the_Roman_Empire" title="Fall of the Roman Empire">remnants of the Roman Empire</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Late_Antiquity#Cities" title="Late Antiquity">cities of late antiquity</a> gained independence but soon lost population and importance. The locus of power in the West shifted to <a href="/wiki/Constantinople" title="Constantinople">Constantinople</a> and to the <a href="/wiki/Early_Muslim_conquests" title="Early Muslim conquests">ascendant Islamic civilization</a> with its major cities <a href="/wiki/Baghdad" title="Baghdad">Baghdad</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cairo" title="Cairo">Cairo</a>, and <a href="/wiki/C%C3%B3rdoba,_Spain" title="C&#243;rdoba, Spain">C&#243;rdoba</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup> From the 9th through the end of the 12th century, <a href="/wiki/Constantinople" title="Constantinople">Constantinople</a>, capital of the <a href="/wiki/Byzantine_Empire" title="Byzantine Empire">Byzantine Empire</a>, was the largest and wealthiest city in Europe, with a population approaching 1 million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman Empire</a> gradually gained <a href="/wiki/List_of_cities_conquered_by_the_Ottoman_Empire" title="List of cities conquered by the Ottoman Empire">control over many cities</a> in the Mediterranean area, including <a href="/wiki/Fall_of_Constantinople" title="Fall of Constantinople">Constantinople in 1453</a>.\n</p><p>In the <a href="/wiki/Holy_Roman_Empire" title="Holy Roman Empire">Holy Roman Empire</a>, beginning in the 12th. century, <a href="/wiki/Free_imperial_city" title="Free imperial city">free imperial cities</a> such as <a href="/wiki/Nuremberg" title="Nuremberg">Nuremberg</a>, <a href="/wiki/Strasbourg" title="Strasbourg">Strasbourg</a>, <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt" title="Frankfurt">Frankfurt</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Zurich" title="Zurich">Zurich</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nijmegen" title="Nijmegen">Nijmegen</a> became a privileged elite among towns having won self-governance from their local lay or secular lord or having been granted self-governanace by the emperor and being placed under his immediate protection. By 1480, these cities, as far as still part of the empire,  became part of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Imperial_Estates" title="Imperial Estates">Imperial Estates</a> governing the empire with the emperor through the <a href="/wiki/Imperial_Diet_(Holy_Roman_Empire)" title="Imperial Diet (Holy Roman Empire)">Imperial Diet</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup>\n</p><p>By the thirteenth and fourteenth centuries, some cities become powerful states, taking surrounding areas under their control or establishing extensive maritime empires. In Italy <a href="/wiki/Medieval_commune" title="Medieval commune">medieval communes</a> developed into <a href="/wiki/Italian_city-states" title="Italian city-states">city-states</a> including the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Venice" title="Republic of Venice">Republic of Venice</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Genoa" title="Republic of Genoa">Republic of Genoa</a>. In Northern Europe, cities including <a href="/wiki/L%C3%BCbeck" title="L&#252;beck">L&#252;beck</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bruges" title="Bruges">Bruges</a> formed the <a href="/wiki/Hanseatic_League" title="Hanseatic League">Hanseatic League</a> for collective defense and commerce. Their power was later <a href="/wiki/Dutch%E2%80%93Hanseatic_War" title="Dutch&#8211;Hanseatic War">challenged</a> and eclipsed by the <a href="/wiki/Burgundian_Netherlands" title="Burgundian Netherlands">Dutch</a> commercial <a href="/wiki/History_of_urban_centers_in_the_Low_Countries" title="History of urban centers in the Low Countries">cities</a> of <a href="/wiki/Ghent" title="Ghent">Ghent</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ypres" title="Ypres">Ypres</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam" title="Amsterdam">Amsterdam</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup>  Similar phenomena existed elsewhere, as in the case of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sakai,_Osaka" title="Sakai, Osaka">Sakai</a>, which enjoyed a considerable autonomy in late medieval Japan.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_modern">Early modern</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=City&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Early modern">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In the West, nation-states became the dominant unit of political organization following the <a href="/wiki/Peace_of_Westphalia" title="Peace of Westphalia">Peace of Westphalia</a> in the seventeenth century.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Blomley2013_72-0"><a href="#cite_note-Blomley2013-72">[72]</a></sup> Western Europe\'s larger capitals (London and Paris) benefited from the growth of commerce following the emergence of an <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Ocean" title="Atlantic Ocean">Atlantic</a> trade. However, most towns remained small.\n</p><p>During the Spanish colonization of the Americas the old Roman city concept was extensively used. Cities were founded in the middle of the newly conquered territories, and were bound to several laws regarding administration, finances and urbanism.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Industrial_age">Industrial age</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=City&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Industrial age">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3><p>\nThe <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Industrial_revolution" title="Industrial revolution">growth of modern industry</a> from the late 18th century onward led to massive <a href="/wiki/Urbanization" title="Urbanization">urbanization</a> and the rise of new great cities, first in Europe and then in other regions, as new opportunities brought huge numbers of migrants from rural communities into urban areas. </p><div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Old_Gyumri_03.PNG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="259" data-file-width="370" decoding="async" height="154" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Old_Gyumri_03.PNG/220px-Old_Gyumri_03.PNG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Old_Gyumri_03.PNG/330px-Old_Gyumri_03.PNG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/d/dc/Old_Gyumri_03.PNG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Old_Gyumri_03.PNG" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Diorama" title="Diorama">Diorama</a> of old <a href="/wiki/Gyumri" title="Gyumri">Gyumri</a>, <a href="/wiki/Armenia" title="Armenia">Armenia</a> with the <a href="/wiki/Holy_Saviour%27s_Church,_Gyumri" title="Holy Saviour\'s Church, Gyumri">Holy Saviour\'s Church</a> (1859&#8211;1873)</div></div></div> <div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Szent_Bertalan_utca_a_Kossuth_Lajos_utca_fel%C3%A9_n%C3%A9zve._Fortepan_721.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1388" data-file-width="2055" decoding="async" height="149" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Szent_Bertalan_utca_a_Kossuth_Lajos_utca_fel%C3%A9_n%C3%A9zve._Fortepan_721.jpg/220px-Szent_Bertalan_utca_a_Kossuth_Lajos_utca_fel%C3%A9_n%C3%A9zve._Fortepan_721.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Szent_Bertalan_utca_a_Kossuth_Lajos_utca_fel%C3%A9_n%C3%A9zve._Fortepan_721.jpg/330px-Szent_Bertalan_utca_a_Kossuth_Lajos_utca_fel%C3%A9_n%C3%A9zve._Fortepan_721.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Szent_Bertalan_utca_a_Kossuth_Lajos_utca_fel%C3%A9_n%C3%A9zve._Fortepan_721.jpg/440px-Szent_Bertalan_utca_a_Kossuth_Lajos_utca_fel%C3%A9_n%C3%A9zve._Fortepan_721.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Szent_Bertalan_utca_a_Kossuth_Lajos_utca_fel%C3%A9_n%C3%A9zve._Fortepan_721.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Small city <a href="/wiki/Gy%C3%B6ngy%C3%B6s" title="Gy&#246;ngy&#246;s">Gy&#246;ngy&#246;s</a> in Hungary in 1938.</div></div></div><p> England led the way as <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a> became the capital of a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/British_empire" title="British empire">world empire</a> and cities across the country grew in locations strategic for <a href="/wiki/Manufacturing" title="Manufacturing">manufacturing</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup> In the United States from 1860 to 1910, the <a href="/wiki/History_of_rail_transport" title="History of rail transport">introduction of railroads</a> reduced transportation costs, and large manufacturing centers began to emerge, fueling migration from rural to city areas.\n</p><p>Industrialized cities became deadly places to live, due to health problems resulting from <a href="/wiki/Overcrowding" title="Overcrowding">overcrowding</a>, <a href="/wiki/Occupational_hazard" title="Occupational hazard">occupational hazards</a> of industry, contaminated water and air, <a href="/wiki/History_of_water_supply_and_sanitation#Modern_age" title="History of water supply and sanitation">poor sanitation</a>, and communicable diseases such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Typhoid" title="Typhoid">typhoid</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cholera" title="Cholera">cholera</a>. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Factories" title="Factories">Factories</a> and <a href="/wiki/Slum" title="Slum">slums</a> emerged as regular features of the urban landscape.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Post-industrial_age">Post-industrial age</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=City&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Post-industrial age">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In the second half of the twentieth century, <a href="/wiki/Deindustrialization" title="Deindustrialization">deindustrialization</a> (or "<a href="/wiki/Economic_restructuring" title="Economic restructuring">economic restructuring</a>") in the West led to <a href="/wiki/Poverty" title="Poverty">poverty</a>, <a href="/wiki/Homelessness" title="Homelessness">homelessness</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Urban_decay" title="Urban decay">urban decay</a> in formerly prosperous cities. America\'s "Steel Belt" became a "<a href="/wiki/Rust_Belt" title="Rust Belt">Rust Belt</a>" and cities such as <a href="/wiki/Decline_of_Detroit" title="Decline of Detroit">Detroit</a>, Michigan, and <a href="/wiki/Gary,_Indiana" title="Gary, Indiana">Gary, Indiana</a> began to <a href="/wiki/Shrinking_cities" title="Shrinking cities">shrink</a>, contrary to the global trend of massive urban expansion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup> Such cities have shifted with varying success into the <a href="/wiki/Service_economy" title="Service economy">service economy</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Public-private_partnerships" title="Public-private partnerships">public-private partnerships</a>, with concomitant <a href="/wiki/Gentrification" title="Gentrification">gentrification</a>, uneven <a href="/wiki/Urban_renewal" title="Urban renewal">revitalization efforts</a>, and selective cultural development.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kaplan2004p164_76-0"><a href="#cite_note-Kaplan2004p164-76">[76]</a></sup> Under the <a href="/wiki/Great_Leap_Forward" title="Great Leap Forward">Great Leap Forward</a> and subsequent <a href="/wiki/Five-year_plans_of_China" title="Five-year plans of China">five-year plans</a> continuing today, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/People%27s_Republic_of_China" title="People\'s Republic of China">People\'s Republic of China</a> has undergone concomitant <a href="/wiki/Urbanization_in_China" title="Urbanization in China">urbanization</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chinese_industrialization" title="Chinese industrialization">industrialization</a> and to become the world\'s leading <a href="/wiki/Manufacturing" title="Manufacturing">manufacturer</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Amidst these economic changes, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/High_technology" title="High technology">high technology</a> and instantaneous <a href="/wiki/Telecommunication" title="Telecommunication">telecommunication</a> enable select cities to become centers of the <a href="/wiki/Knowledge_economy" title="Knowledge economy">knowledge economy</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup> A new <a href="/wiki/Smart_city" title="Smart city">smart city</a> paradigm, supported by institutions such as the <a href="/wiki/RAND_Corporation" title="RAND Corporation">RAND Corporation</a> and <a href="/wiki/IBM" title="IBM">IBM</a>, is bringing computerized <a href="/wiki/Surveillance_issues_in_smart_cities" title="Surveillance issues in smart cities">surveillance</a>, data analysis, and <a href="/wiki/E-governance" title="E-governance">governance</a> to bear on cities and city-dwellers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup> Some companies are building brand new <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Land_use_planning" title="Land use planning">masterplanned</a> cities from scratch on <a href="/wiki/Greenfield_land" title="Greenfield land">greenfield</a> sites.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Urbanization">Urbanization</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=City&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Urbanization">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Urbanization" title="Urbanization">Urbanization</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Jakarta_slumhome_2.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1920" data-file-width="2560" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Jakarta_slumhome_2.jpg/220px-Jakarta_slumhome_2.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Jakarta_slumhome_2.jpg/330px-Jakarta_slumhome_2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Jakarta_slumhome_2.jpg/440px-Jakarta_slumhome_2.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Jakarta_slumhome_2.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Clothes hang neatly and visibly in these <a href="/wiki/Jakarta" title="Jakarta">Jakarta</a> dwellings on the water near a <a href="/wiki/Waste" title="Waste">dump</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Urbanization" title="Urbanization">Urbanization</a> is the process of migration from rural into urban areas, driven by various political, economic, and cultural factors. Until the 18th century, an equilibrium existed between the rural agricultural population and towns featuring <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Market_(place)" title="Market (place)">markets</a> and small-scale manufacturing.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FreyZimmer2001_84-0"><a href="#cite_note-FreyZimmer2001-84">[84]</a></sup> With the <a href="/wiki/British_Agricultural_Revolution" title="British Agricultural Revolution">agricultural</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Industrial_revolution" title="Industrial revolution">industrial</a> revolutions urban population began its unprecedented growth, both through migration and through <a href="/wiki/Demographic_transition" title="Demographic transition">demographic expansion</a>. In <a href="/wiki/England" title="England">England</a> the proportion of the population living in cities jumped from 17% in 1801 to 72% in 1891.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-urbanization_85-0"><a href="#cite_note-urbanization-85">[85]</a></sup> In 1900, 15% of the world population lived in cities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup> The cultural appeal of cities also plays a role in attracting residents.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MoholyNagy1968p136_87-0"><a href="#cite_note-MoholyNagy1968p136-87">[87]</a></sup>\n</p><p>\nUrbanization rapidly spread across the Europe and the Americas and since the 1950s has taken hold in Asia and Africa as well. The Population Division of the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Department_of_Economic_and_Social_Affairs" title="United Nations Department of Economic and Social Affairs">United Nations Department of Economic and Social Affairs</a>, reported in 2014 that for the first time more than half of the world population lives in cities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SenguptaUN2014_88-0"><a href="#cite_note-SenguptaUN2014-88">[88]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[a]</a></sup> </p><div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Historical_global_urban_-_rural_population_trends.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1037" data-file-width="1426" decoding="async" height="160" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Historical_global_urban_-_rural_population_trends.png/220px-Historical_global_urban_-_rural_population_trends.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Historical_global_urban_-_rural_population_trends.png/330px-Historical_global_urban_-_rural_population_trends.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Historical_global_urban_-_rural_population_trends.png/440px-Historical_global_urban_-_rural_population_trends.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Historical_global_urban_-_rural_population_trends.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Graph showing urbanization from 1950 projected to 2050.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[95]</a></sup></div></div></div><p> Latin America is the most urban continent, with four fifths of its population living in cities, including one fifth of the population said to live in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shantytown" title="Shantytown">shantytowns</a> (<a href="/wiki/Favela" title="Favela">favelas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Campamento_(Chile)" title="Campamento (Chile)">poblaciones callampas</a>, etc.).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[96]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Batam" title="Batam">Batam</a>, Indonesia, <a href="/wiki/Mogadishu" title="Mogadishu">Mogadishu</a>, Somalia, <a href="/wiki/Xiamen" title="Xiamen">Xiamen</a>, China and <a href="/wiki/Niamey" title="Niamey">Niamey</a>, Niger, are considered among the world\'s fastest-growing cities, with annual growth rates of 5&#8211;8%.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[97]</a></sup> In general, the <a href="/wiki/Developed_country" title="Developed country">more developed countries</a> of the "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Global_North" title="Global North">Global North</a>" remain more urbanized than the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Less_developed_countries" title="Less developed countries">less developed countries</a> of the "<a href="/wiki/Global_South" title="Global South">Global South</a>"&#8212;but the difference continues to shrink because urbanization is happening faster in the latter group. Asia is home to by far the greatest absolute number of city-dwellers: over two billion and counting.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FreyZimmer2001_84-1"><a href="#cite_note-FreyZimmer2001-84">[84]</a></sup> The UN predicts an additional 2.5 billion citydwellers (and 300 million fewer countrydwellers) worldwide by 2050, with 90% of urban population expansion occurring in Asia and Africa.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SenguptaUN2014_88-1"><a href="#cite_note-SenguptaUN2014-88">[88]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[98]</a></sup>\n</p><p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Megacities" title="Megacities">Megacities</a>, cities with population in the multi-millions, have proliferated into the dozens, arising especially in Asia, Africa, and Latin America.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[99]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101">[100]</a></sup> Economic globalization fuels the growth of these cities, as new torrents of foreign <a href="/wiki/Financial_capital" title="Financial capital">capital</a> arrange for rapid industrialization, as well as <a href="/wiki/Offshoring" title="Offshoring">relocation of major businesses</a> from Europe and North America, attracting <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Immigrant" title="Immigrant">immigrants</a> from near and far.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102">[101]</a></sup> A deep gulf divides rich and poor in these cities, with usually contain a super-wealthy elite living in <a href="/wiki/Gated_community" title="Gated community">gated communities</a> and large masses of people living in substandard housing with inadequate infrastructure and otherwise poor conditions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103">[102]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Cities around the world have expanded physically as they grow in population, with increases in their surface extent, with the creation of high-rise buildings for residential and commercial use, and with development underground.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104"><a href="#cite_note-104">[103]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105">[104]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Urbanization can create rapid demand for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Water_resources_management" title="Water resources management">water resources management</a>, as formerly good sources of freshwater become overused and polluted, and the volume of <a href="/wiki/Sewage" title="Sewage">sewage</a> begins to exceed manageable levels.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bakker2003_106-0"><a href="#cite_note-Bakker2003-106">[105]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Government">Government</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=City&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Government">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Local_government" title="Local government">Local government</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:City_Council_of_Tehran,_17_September_2015.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="481" data-file-width="800" decoding="async" height="132" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/City_Council_of_Tehran%2C_17_September_2015.jpg/220px-City_Council_of_Tehran%2C_17_September_2015.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/City_Council_of_Tehran%2C_17_September_2015.jpg/330px-City_Council_of_Tehran%2C_17_September_2015.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/City_Council_of_Tehran%2C_17_September_2015.jpg/440px-City_Council_of_Tehran%2C_17_September_2015.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:City_Council_of_Tehran,_17_September_2015.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/City_council" title="City council">city council</a> of <a href="/wiki/Tehran" title="Tehran">Tehran</a> meets in September 2015.</div></div></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Local_government" title="Local government">Local government</a> of cities takes different forms including prominently the <a href="/wiki/Municipality" title="Municipality">municipality</a> (especially <a href="/wiki/Local_government_in_England" title="Local government in England">in England</a>, <a href="/wiki/Local_government_in_the_United_States" title="Local government in the United States">in the United States</a>, <a href="/wiki/Municipal_governance_in_India" title="Municipal governance in India">in India</a>, and in other <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Crown_colonies" title="Crown colonies">British colonies</a>; legally, the <a href="/wiki/Municipal_corporation" title="Municipal corporation">municipal corporation</a>;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107">[106]</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Municipio" title="Municipio">municipio</a></i> in <a href="/wiki/Municipalities_of_Spain" title="Municipalities of Spain">Spain</a> and <a href="/wiki/Municipalities_of_Portugal" title="Municipalities of Portugal">in Portugal</a>, and, along with <i><a href="/wiki/Municipalidad" title="Municipalidad">municipalidad</a></i>, in most former parts of the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Empire" title="Spanish Empire">Spanish</a> and <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Empire" title="Portuguese Empire">Portuguese</a> empires) and the <i>commune</i> (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Communes_in_France" title="Communes in France">in France</a> and <a href="/wiki/Communes_of_Chile" title="Communes of Chile">in Chile</a>; or <i><a href="/wiki/Comune" title="Comune">comune</a></i> in Italy).\n</p><p>The chief official of the city has the title of <a href="/wiki/Mayor" title="Mayor">mayor</a>. Whatever their true degree of political authority, the mayor typically acts as the <a href="/wiki/Figurehead" title="Figurehead">figurehead</a> or personification of their city.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108">[107]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Penang_City_Hall.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1280" data-file-width="2048" decoding="async" height="138" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Penang_City_Hall.jpg/220px-Penang_City_Hall.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Penang_City_Hall.jpg/330px-Penang_City_Hall.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Penang_City_Hall.jpg/440px-Penang_City_Hall.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Penang_City_Hall.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/City_Hall,_Penang" title="City Hall, Penang">The city hall</a> in <a href="/wiki/George_Town,_Penang" title="George Town, Penang">George Town</a>, Malaysia, today serves as the <a href="/wiki/Seat_of_local_government" title="Seat of local government">seat</a> of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/City_Council_of_Penang_Island" title="City Council of Penang Island">City Council of Penang Island</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109">[108]</a></sup></div></div></div>\n<p>City governments have authority to make <a href="/wiki/Law" title="Law">laws</a> governing activity within cities, while its <a href="/wiki/Jurisdiction" title="Jurisdiction">jurisdiction</a> is generally considered <a href="/wiki/Conflict_of_laws" title="Conflict of laws">subordinate</a> (in ascending order) to <a href="/wiki/State_government" title="State government">state/provincial</a>, <a href="/wiki/Central_government" title="Central government">national</a>, and perhaps <a href="/wiki/International_law" title="International law">international law</a>. This hierarchy of law is not enforced rigidly in practice&#8212;for example in conflicts between municipal regulations and national principles such as <a href="/wiki/Constitutional_right" title="Constitutional right">constitutional rights</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Property_rights" title="Property rights">property rights</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Blomley2013_72-1"><a href="#cite_note-Blomley2013-72">[72]</a></sup> Legal conflicts and issues arise more frequently in cities than elsewhere due to the bare fact of their greater density.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110">[109]</a></sup> Modern city governments thoroughly <a href="/wiki/Regulation" title="Regulation">regulate</a> <a href="/wiki/Everyday_life" title="Everyday life">everyday life</a> in many dimensions, including <a href="/wiki/Public_health" title="Public health">public</a> and personal <a href="/wiki/Health" title="Health">health</a>, <a href="/wiki/Transport" title="Transport">transport</a>, <a href="/wiki/Burial" title="Burial">burial</a>, <a href="/wiki/Resource" title="Resource">resource</a> use and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Resource_extraction" title="Resource extraction">extraction</a>, <a href="/wiki/Recreation" title="Recreation">recreation</a>, and the nature and use of <a href="/wiki/Building" title="Building">buildings</a>. Technologies, techniques, and laws governing these areas&#8212;developed in cities&#8212;have become ubiquitous in many areas.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111">[110]</a></sup>\nMunicipal officials may be appointed from a higher level of government or elected locally.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112"><a href="#cite_note-112">[111]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Municipal_services">Municipal services</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=City&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Municipal services">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Aftermath_of_a_huge_fire_at_Thomas_McKenzie_%26_Sons_Ltd._on_Pearse_Street,_Dublin.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1347" data-file-width="2000" decoding="async" height="148" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Aftermath_of_a_huge_fire_at_Thomas_McKenzie_%26_Sons_Ltd._on_Pearse_Street%2C_Dublin.jpg/220px-Aftermath_of_a_huge_fire_at_Thomas_McKenzie_%26_Sons_Ltd._on_Pearse_Street%2C_Dublin.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Aftermath_of_a_huge_fire_at_Thomas_McKenzie_%26_Sons_Ltd._on_Pearse_Street%2C_Dublin.jpg/330px-Aftermath_of_a_huge_fire_at_Thomas_McKenzie_%26_Sons_Ltd._on_Pearse_Street%2C_Dublin.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Aftermath_of_a_huge_fire_at_Thomas_McKenzie_%26_Sons_Ltd._on_Pearse_Street%2C_Dublin.jpg/440px-Aftermath_of_a_huge_fire_at_Thomas_McKenzie_%26_Sons_Ltd._on_Pearse_Street%2C_Dublin.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Aftermath_of_a_huge_fire_at_Thomas_McKenzie_%26_Sons_Ltd._on_Pearse_Street,_Dublin.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Dublin_Fire_Brigade" title="Dublin Fire Brigade">Dublin Fire Brigade</a> pictured in April 1970, quenching a severe fire at a hardware store.</div></div></div>\n<p>Cities typically provide <a href="/wiki/Municipal_services" title="Municipal services">municipal services</a> such as <a href="/wiki/Education" title="Education">education</a>, through <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/School_system" title="School system">school systems</a>; <a href="/wiki/Police" title="Police">policing</a>, through police departments; and <a href="/wiki/Firefighting" title="Firefighting">firefighting</a>, through <a href="/wiki/Fire_department" title="Fire department">fire departments</a>; as well as the city\'s basic
